brickout-game.py
1 """
2  Pygame base template for opening a window
3  
4  Sample Python/Pygame Programs
5  Simpson College Computer Science
6  http://programarcadegames.com/
7  http://simpson.edu/computer-science/
8  
9  Explanation video: http://youtu.be/vRB_983kUMc
10 
11 -------------------------------------------------
12 
13 Author for the Brickout game is Christian Bender
14 That includes the classes Ball, Paddle, Brick, and BrickWall.
15 
16 """
17  
18 import pygame
19 import random
20 
21  
22 # Define some colors
23 BLACK = (0, 0, 0)
24 WHITE = (255, 255, 255)
25 GREEN = (0, 255, 0)
26 RED = (255, 0, 0)
27 
28 pygame.init()
29 
30 # Set the width and height of the screen [width, height]
31 size = (700, 500)
32 screen = pygame.display.set_mode(size)
33 
34 """
35     This is a simple Ball class for respresenting a ball 
36     in the game. 
37 """
38 class Ball(object):
39     def __init__ (self, screen, radius,x,y):
40         self.__screen = screen
41         self._radius = radius
42         self._xLoc = x
43         self._yLoc = y
44         self.__xVel = 7
45         self.__yVel = 2
46         w, h = pygame.display.get_surface().get_size()
47         self.__width = w
48         self.__height = h
49     def getXVel(self):
50         return self.__xVel
51     def getYVel(self):
52         return self.__yVel
53     def draw(self):
54         """
55             draws the ball onto screen.
56         """
57         pygame.draw.circle(screen,(255, 0, 0) , (self._xLoc,self._yLoc), self._radius)
58     def update(self, paddle, brickwall):
59         """
60             moves the ball at the screen.
61             contains some collision detection.
62         """
63         self._xLoc += self.__xVel
64         self._yLoc += self.__yVel
65         #left screen wall bounce
66         if self._xLoc <= self._radius:
67             self.__xVel *= -1
68         #right screen wall bounce
69         elif self._xLoc >= self.__width - self._radius:
70             self.__xVel *= -1
71         #top wall bounce
72         if self._yLoc <= self._radius:
73             self.__yVel *= -1
74         #bottom drop out
75         elif self._yLoc >= self.__width - self._radius:
76             return True
77 
78         # for bouncing off the bricks.
79         if brickwall.collide(self):
80             self.__yVel *= -1
81 
82         # collision detection between ball and paddle.
83         paddleX = paddle._xLoc
84         paddleY = paddle._yLoc
85         paddleW = paddle._width
86         paddleH = paddle._height
87         ballX = self._xLoc
88         ballY = self._yLoc
89 
90         if ((ballX + self._radius) >= paddleX and ballX <= (paddleX + paddleW)) \
91         and ((ballY + self._radius) >= paddleY and ballY <= (paddleY + paddleH)):
92             self.__yVel *= -1
93 
94         return False
95 
96         
97 """
98     Simple class for representing a paddle
99 """        
100 class Paddle (object):
101     def __init__ (self, screen, width, height,x,y):
102         self.__screen = screen
103         self._width = width
104         self._height = height
105         self._xLoc = x
106         self._yLoc = y
107         w, h = pygame.display.get_surface().get_size()
108         self.__W = w
109         self.__H = h
110     def draw(self):
111         """
112             draws the paddle onto screen.
113         """
114         pygame.draw.rect(screen, (0,0,0), (self._xLoc,self._yLoc,self._width,self._height),0)
115     def update(self):
116         """
117             moves the paddle at the screen via mouse
118         """
119         x,y = pygame.mouse.get_pos()
120         if x >= 0 and x <= (self.__W - self._width):
121             self._xLoc = x
122  
123 """
124     This class represents a simple Brick class.
125     For representing bricks onto screen.
126 """
127 class Brick (pygame.sprite.Sprite):
128     def __init__(self, screen, width, height, x,y):
129         self.__screen = screen
130         self._width = width
131         self._height = height
132         self._xLoc = x
133         self._yLoc = y
134         w, h = pygame.display.get_surface().get_size()
135         self.__W = w
136         self.__H = h
137         self.__isInGroup = False
138     def draw(self):
139         """
140             draws the brick onto screen.
141             color: rgb(56, 177, 237)
142         """
143         pygame.draw.rect(screen, (56, 177, 237), (self._xLoc,self._yLoc,self._width,self._height),0)
144     def add (self, group):
145         """
146             adds this brick to a given group.
147         """
148         group.add(self)
149         self.__isInGroup = True
150     def remove(self, group):
151         """
152             removes this brick from the given group.
153         """
154         group.remove(self)
155         self.__isInGroup = False
156     def alive(self):
157         """
158             returns true when this brick belongs to the brick wall.
159             otherwise false
160         """
161         return self.__isInGroup
162 
163     def collide(self, ball):
164         """
165             collision detection between ball and this brick
166         """
167         brickX = self._xLoc
168         brickY = self._yLoc
169         brickW = self._width
170         brickH = self._height
171         ballX = ball._xLoc
172         ballY = ball._yLoc
173         ballXVel = ball.getXVel()
174         ballYVel = ball.getYVel()
175 
176 
177         if ((ballX + ball._radius) >= brickX and (ballX+ball._radius) <= (brickX + brickW)) \
178         and ((ballY - ball._radius) >= brickY and (ballY - ball._radius)\
179              <= (brickY + brickH)):
180             return True
181         else:
182             return False
183 
184 
185 """
186     This is a simple class for representing a 
187     brick wall.
188 """
189 class BrickWall (pygame.sprite.Group):
190     def __init__ (self,screen, x, y, width, height):
191         self.__screen = screen
192         self._x = x
193         self._y = y
194         self._width = width
195         self._height = height
196         self._bricks = []
197 
198         X = x
199         Y = y
200         for i in range(3):
201             for j in range(4):
202                 self._bricks.append(Brick(screen,width,height,X,Y))
203                 X += width + (width/ 7.0)
204             Y += height + (height / 7.0)
205             X = x
206         
207     def add(self,brick):
208         """
209             adds a brick to this BrickWall (group)
210         """
211         self._bricks.append(brick)
212     def remove(self,brick):
213         """
214             removes a brick from this BrickWall (group)
215         """
216         self._bricks.remove(brick)
217     def draw(self):
218         """
219             draws all bricks onto screen.
220         """
221         for brick in self._bricks:
222             if brick != None:
223                 brick.draw()
224     def update(self, ball):
225         """
226             checks collision between ball and bricks.
227         """
228         for i in range(len(self._bricks)):
229             if ((self._bricks[i] != None) and self._bricks[i].collide(ball)):
230                 self._bricks[i] = None
231         
232         # removes the None-elements from the brick list.
233         for brick in self._bricks:
234             if brick == None:
235                 self._bricks.remove(brick)
236     def hasWin(self):
237         """
238             Has player win the game?
239         """
240         return len(self._bricks) == 0
241     def collide (self, ball):
242         """
243             check collisions between the ball and 
244             any of the bricks.
245         """
246         for brick in self._bricks:
247             if brick.collide(ball):
248                 return True
249         return False
250 
251 # The game objects ball, paddle and brick wall
252 ball = Ball(screen,25, random.randint(1,700),250)
253 paddle = Paddle(screen,100,20,250,450)
254 brickWall = BrickWall(screen,25,25,150,50)
255 
256 isGameOver = False # determines whether game is lose
257 gameStatus = True # game is still running
258 
259 score = 0 # score for the game.
260  
261 pygame.display.set_caption("Brickout-game")
262  
263 # Loop until the user clicks the close button.
264 done = False
265  
266 # Used to manage how fast the screen updates
267 clock = pygame.time.Clock()
268 
269 # for displaying text in the game 
270 pygame.font.init() # you have to call this at the start, 
271                    # if you want to use this module.
272 
273 # message for game over
274 mgGameOver = pygame.font.SysFont('Comic Sans MS', 40)
275 
276 # message for winning the game.
277 mgWin = pygame.font.SysFont('Comic Sans MS', 40)
278 
279 # message for score
280 mgScore = pygame.font.SysFont('Comic Sans MS', 40)
281 
282 textsurfaceGameOver = mgGameOver.render('Game Over!', False, (0, 0, 0))
283 textsurfaceWin = mgWin.render("You win!",False,(0,0,0))
284 textsurfaceScore = mgScore.render("score: "+str(score),False,(0,0,0))
285    
286  
287 # -------- Main Program Loop -----------
288 while not done:
289     # --- Main event loop
290     for event in pygame.event.get():
291         if event.type == pygame.QUIT:
292             done = True
293  
294     # --- Game logic should go here
295  
296     # --- Screen-clearing code goes here
297  
298     # Here, we clear the screen to white. Don't put other drawing commands
299     # above this, or they will be erased with this command.
300  
301     # If you want a background image, replace this clear with blit'ing the
302     # background image.
303     screen.fill(WHITE)
304  
305     # --- Drawing code should go here
306     
307     """
308         Because I use OOP in the game logic and the drawing code,
309         are both in the same section.
310     """
311     if gameStatus:
312 
313         # first draws ball for appropriate displaying the score. 
314         brickWall.draw()
315 
316          # for counting and displaying the score
317         if brickWall.collide(ball):
318             score += 10
319         textsurfaceScore = mgScore.render("score: "+str(score),False,(0,0,0))
320         screen.blit(textsurfaceScore,(300,0))
321 
322         # after scoring. because hit bricks are removed in the update-method
323         brickWall.update(ball)
324 
325         paddle.draw()
326         paddle.update()
327 
328         if ball.update(paddle, brickWall):
329             isGameOver = True
330             gameStatus = False
331         
332         if brickWall.hasWin():
333             gameStatus = False
334 
335         ball.draw()
336 
337     else: # game isn't running.
338         if isGameOver: # player lose
339             screen.blit(textsurfaceGameOver,(0,0))
340             textsurfaceScore = mgScore.render("score: "+str(score),False,(0,0,0))
341             screen.blit(textsurfaceScore,(300,0))
342         elif brickWall.hasWin(): # player win
343             screen.blit(textsurfaceWin,(0,0))
344             textsurfaceScore = mgScore.render("score: "+str(score),False,(0,0,0))
345             screen.blit(textsurfaceScore,(300,0))
346      
347     # --- Go ahead and update the screen with what we've drawn.
348     pygame.display.flip()
349  
350     # --- Limit to 60 frames per second
351     clock.tick(60)
352  
353 # Close the window and quit.
354 pygame.quit()
================
calculator.py
1 """
2 Written by  : Shreyas Daniel - github.com/shreydan
3 Description : Uses Pythons eval() function
4               as a way to implement calculator.
5              
6 Functions available are:
7 --------------------------------------------
8                          + : addition
9                          - : subtraction
10                          * : multiplication
11                          / : division
12                          % : percentage
13                          e : 2.718281...
14                         pi : 3.141592... 
15                       sine : sin(rad)
16                     cosine : cos(rad)
17                    tangent : tan(rad)
18                  remainder : XmodY
19                square root : sqrt(n)
20   round to nearest integer : round(n)
21 convert degrees to radians : rad(deg)
22 """
23 
24 import math
25 import sys
26 
27 
28 def calc(term):
29     """
30         input: term of type str
31         output: returns the result of the computed term.
32         purpose: This function is the actual calculator and the heart of the application
33     """
34     
35     # This part is for reading and converting arithmetic terms.
36     term = term.replace(' ', '')
37     term = term.replace('^', '**')
38     term = term.replace('=', '')
39     term = term.replace('?', '')
40     term = term.replace('%', '/100')
41     term = term.replace('rad', 'radians')
42     term = term.replace('mod', '%')
43 
44     functions = ['sin', 'cos', 'tan', 'cosh', 'sinh', 'tanh', 'sqrt', 'pi', 'radians', 'e'] 
45 
46     # This part is for reading and converting function expressions.
47     term = term.lower()
48     
49     for function in functions:            
50         if function in term:
51             withmath = 'math.' + function
52             term = term.replace(function, withmath)
53 
54     try:
55 
56         # here goes the actual evaluating.
57         term = eval(term)
58 
59     # here goes to the error cases.
60     except ZeroDivisionError:
61 
62         print("Can't divide by 0.  Please try again.")
63 
64     except NameError:
65 
66         print('Invalid input.  Please try again')
67 
68     except AttributeError:
69 
70         print('Please check usage method and try again.')
71         
72     return term
73 
74 
75 def result(term):
76     """
77         input:  term of type str
78         output: none
79         purpose: passes the argument to the function calc(...) and 
80                 prints the result onto console.
81     """
82     print("\n" + str(calc(term)))
83 
84 
85 def main():
86     """
87         main-program
88         purpose: handles user input and prints 
89                  information to the console.
90     """
91     
92     print("\nScientific Calculator\n\nFor Example: sin(rad(90)) + 50% * (sqrt(16)) + round(1.42^2)"+\
93           "- 12mod3\n\nEnter quit to exit")
94

check_file.py
1 # Script Name		: check_file.py
2 
3 # Author		: Craig Richards
4 # Created		: 20 May 2013
5 # Last Modified		:
6 # Version		: 1.0
7 
8 # Modifications	: with statement added to ensure correct file closure
9 
10 # Description	: Check a file exists and that we can read the file
11 from __future__ import print_function
12 import sys		# Import the Modules
13 import os		# Import the Modules
14 
15 # Prints usage if not appropriate length of arguments are provided
16 
17 
18 def usage():
19     print('[-] Usage: python check_file.py [filename1] [filename2] ... [filenameN]')
20 
21 
22 # Readfile Functions which open the file that is passed to the script
23 def readfile(filename):
24     with open(filename, 'r') as f:      # Ensure file is correctly closed under
25         file = f.read()                 # all circumstances
26     print(file)
27     print()
28     print('#'*80)
29     print()
30 
31 def main():
32     # Check the arguments passed to the script
33     if len(sys.argv) >= 2:
34         filenames = sys.argv[1:]
35         filteredfilenames_1 = list(filenames)   #To counter changing in the same list which you are iterating
36         filteredfilenames_2 = list(filenames)
37         # Iterate for each filename passed in command line argument
38         for filename in filteredfilenames_1:
39             if not os.path.isfile(filename):		# Check the File exists
40                 print('[-] ' + filename + ' does not exist.')
41                 filteredfilenames_2.remove(filename)			#remove non existing files from fileNames list
42                 continue
43 
44             # Check you can read the file
45             if not os.access(filename, os.R_OK):
46                 print('[-] ' + filename + ' access denied')
47                 # remove non readable fileNames
48                 filteredfilenames_2.remove(filename)
49                 continue
50 
51         # Read the content of each file that both exists and is readable
52         for filename in filteredfilenames_2:
53             # Display Message and read the file contents
54             print('[+] Reading from : ' + filename)
55             readfile(filename)
56 
57     else:
58         usage() # Print usage if not all parameters passed/Checked
59 
60 
61 if __name__ == '__main__':
62     main()

check_for_sqlite_files.py
1 # Script Name	: check_for_sqlite_files.py
2 # Author		: Craig Richards
3 # Created		: 07 June 2013
4 # Last Modified	: 14 February 2016
5 # Version		: 1.0.1
6 
7 # Modifications	: 1.0.1 - Remove unecessary line and variable on Line 21
8 
9 # Description	: Scans directories to check if there are any sqlite files in there 
10 
11 from __future__ import print_function
12 import os
13 
14 def isSQLite3(filename):
15     from os.path import isfile, getsize
16 
17     if not isfile(filename):
18         return False
19     if getsize(filename) < 100: # SQLite database file header is 100 bytes
20         return False
21     else:
22         fd = open(filename, 'rb')
23         Header = fd.read(100)
24         fd.close()
25 
26         if Header[0:16] == 'SQLite format 3\000':
27             return True
28         else:
29             return False
30 
31 log=open('sqlite_audit.txt','w')
32 for r,d,f in os.walk(r'.'):
33   for files in f:
34     if isSQLite3(files):
35       print(files)
36       print("[+] '%s' **** is a SQLITE database file **** " % os.path.join(r,files))
37       log.write("[+] '%s' **** is a SQLITE database file **** " % files+'\n')
38     else:
39       log.write("[-] '%s' is NOT a sqlite database file" % os.path.join(r,files)+'\n')
40       log.write("[-] '%s' is NOT a sqlite database file" % files+'\n')================
check_input.py
1 def get_user_input(start,end):
2 
3     """
4         input: two integer values
5                lower limit 'start' and maximum 'end'
6                the arguments aren't inclusive.
7 
8         output: if reading successful then returns the read integer. 
9 
10         purpose: reads from command-line a integer in the given bounds. 
11                  while input invalid asks user again
12     """
13 
14     loop = True # controls while-loop
15 
16     while (loop):
17 
18         try:
19 
20             # reads and converts the input from the console. 
21             userInput = int(input("Enter Your choice: "))
22 
23             # checks whether input is in the given bounds.
24             if userInput > end  or userInput < start:
25 
26                 # error case
27                 print("Please try again. Not in valid bounds.")
28 
29             else:
30 
31                 # valid case
32                 loop = False # aborts while-loop
33 
34         except ValueError:
35 
36             # error case
37             print("Please try again. Only numbers") 
38 
39     return userInput
40

chicks_n_rabs.py
1 '''Author Anurag Kumar(mailto:anuragkumarak95@gmail.com)
2 
3 Module to solve a classic ancient Chinese puzzle:
4 We count 35 heads and 94 legs among the chickens and rabbits in a farm. 
5 How many rabbits and how many chickens do we have?
6 
7 
8 '''
9 def solve(numheads,numlegs):
10     ns='No solutions!'
11     for i in range(numheads+1):
12         j=numheads-i
13         if 2*i+4*j==numlegs:
14             return i,j
15     return ns,ns
16 
17 if __name__=="__main__":
18     numheads=35
19     numlegs=94
20 
21     solutions=solve(numheads,numlegs)
22     print(solutions)

dice.py
1 # Script Name	: dice.py
2 # Author		: Craig Richards
3 # Created		: 05th February 2017
4 # Last Modified	: 
5 # Version		: 1.0
6 
7 # Modifications	:
8 
9 # Description	: This will randomly select two numbers, like throwing dice, you can change the sides of the dice if you wish
10 
11 import random
12 class Die(object):
13   #A dice has a feature of number about how many sides it has when it's established,like 6.
14   def __init__(self):
15     self.sides=6
16     
17   """because a dice contains at least 4 planes.
18   So use this method to give it a judgement when you need to change the instance attributes."""
19   def set_sides(self, sides_change):
20     if sides_change>=4:
21       if sides_change != 6:
22         print("change sides from 6 to ",sides_change," !")
23       else:  # added else clause for printing a message that sides set to 6
24           print ("sides set to 6")
25       self.sides = sides_change
26     else:
27       print("wrong sides! sides set to 6")
28       
29   def roll(self):
30     return random.randint(1, self.sides)
31 
32 d = Die()
33 d1 = Die()
34 d.set_sides(4)
35 d1.set_sides(4)
36 print (d.roll(), d1.roll())

diceV2_dynamic.py
1 
2 
3 
4 
5 import random
6 #Class that that holds dice-functions. You can set the amount of sides and roll with each dice object.
7 class Dice():
8     def __init__(self):
9         self.sideCount=6
10      
11     def setSides(self, sides):
12         if sides > 3:
13             self.sides = sides
14         else:
15             print("This absolutely shouldn't ever happen. The programmer sucks or someone has tweaked with code they weren't supposed to touch!")
16       
17     def roll(self):
18         return random.randint(1, self.sides)
19 
20 
21 ###=====================================================================
22 
23 
24 #Checks to make sure that the input is actually an integer. 
25 #This implementation can be improved greatly of course.
26 def checkInput(sides):
27     try:
28         if int(sides) != 0:
29             if (float(sides)%int(sides) == 0): #excludes the possibility of inputted floats being rounded.
30                 return int(sides)
31         else:
32             return int(sides)
33     
34     except:
35         print("Invalid input!")
36         return None
37 
38 
39 #Picks a number that is at least of a certain size. 
40 #That means in this program, the dices being possible to use in 3 dimensional space. 
41 def pickNumber(item, questionString, lowerlimit): 
42     while True:
43         item = input(questionString)
44         item = checkInput(item)
45         if type(item) == int:
46             if item <= lowerlimit:
47                 print("Input too low!")
48                 continue
49             else:
50                 return item
51 
52 
53 #Main-function of the program that sets up the dices for the user as they want them. 
54 def getDices(): 
55     dices = []
56     sides = None
57     diceAmount = None
58     sideLowerLimit = 3 #Do Not Touch!
59     diceLowerLimit = 1 #Do Not Touch!
60 
61     sides = pickNumber(sides, "How many sides will the dices have?: ", sideLowerLimit)
62     diceAmount = pickNumber(diceAmount, "How many dices will do you want?: ", diceLowerLimit)
63 
64     for i in range(0, diceAmount):
65         d = Dice()
66         d.setSides(sides)
67         dices.append(d) 
68 
69     return dices
70 
71 
72 
73 dices = getDices()
74 #=================================================================
75 #Output section.
76 
77 
78 rollOutput = ""
79 
80 for dice in dices:
81     rollOutput = rollOutput + str(dice.roll()) + ", "
82 
83 rollOutput = rollOutput[:-2]
84 print (rollOutput)

factorial_perm_comp.py
1 # Script Name		: factorial_perm_comp.py
2 # Author			: Ebiwari Williams
3 # Created			: 20th May 2017
4 # Last Modified		: 
5 # Version			: 1.0
6 
7 # Modifications		: 
8 
9 # Description		: Find Factorial, Permutation and Combination of a Number
10 
11 
12 def factorial(n):	
13 	fact = 1
14 	while(n >= 1 ): 
15 		fact = fact * n 
16 		n = n - 1
17 
18 	return fact
19 
20 
21 def permutation(n,r):
22 	return factorial(n)/factorial(n-r)
23 
24 
25 
26 def combination(n,r):
27 	return permutation(n,r)/factorial(r)
28 
29 
30 def main():
31 	print('choose between operator 1,2,3')
32 	print('1) Factorial')
33 	print('2) Permutation')
34 	print('3) Combination')
35 
36 	operation = input('\n')
37 
38 	if(operation ==  '1'):
39 		print('Factorial Computation\n')
40 		while(True):
41 			try:
42 				n = int(input('\n Enter  Value for n '))
43 				print('Factorial of {} = {}'.format(n,factorial(n)))
44 				break
45 			except(ValueError):
46 				print('Invalid Value')
47 				continue
48 
49 	elif(operation == '2'):
50 		print('Permutation Computation\n')
51 
52 		while(True):
53 			try:
54 				n  = int(input('\n Enter Value for n '))
55 				r  = int(input('\n Enter Value for r '))
56 				print('Permutation of {}P{} = {}'.format(n,r,permutation(n,r)))
57 				break
58 			except(ValueError):
59 				print('Invalid Value')
60 				continue
61 
62 
63 	elif(operation == '3'):
64 		print('Combination Computation\n')
65 		while(True):
66 			try:
67 				n  = int(input('\n Enter Value for n '))
68 				r  = int(input('\n Enter Value for r '))
69 
70 				print('Combination of {}C{} = {}'.format(n,r,combination(n,r)))
71 				break
72 
73 			except(ValueError):
74 				print('Invalid Value')
75 				continue
76 
77 
78 if __name__ == '__main__':
79 	main()
================

9 
10 
11 # get file information using os.stat()
12 # tested with Python24 vegsaeat 25sep2006
13 from __future__ import print_function
14 import os
15 import sys
16 import stat   # index constants for os.stat()
17 import time
18 
19 if sys.version_info >= (3, 0):
20     raw_input = input
21 
22 try_count = 16
23 
24 while try_count:
25     file_name = raw_input("Enter a file name: ")      # pick a file you have
26     fhand = open(file_name)
27     count = 0
28     for lines in fhand:
29         count = count + 1
30     fhand = open(file_name)
31     inp = fhand.read()
32     t_char = len(inp) 
33     try_count >>= 1
34     try:
35         file_stats = os.stat(file_name)
36         print ("This is os.stat",file_stats)
37         break
38     except OSError:
39         print ("\nNameError : [%s] No such file or directory\n", file_name)
40

42     print ("Trial limit exceeded \nExiting program")
43     sys.exit()
44

46 file_info = {
47     'fname': file_name,
48     'fsize': file_stats[stat.ST_SIZE],
49     'f_lm' : time.strftime("%d/%m/%Y %I:%M:%S %p",
50                            time.localtime(file_stats[stat.ST_MTIME])),
51     'f_la' : time.strftime("%d/%m/%Y %I:%M:%S %p",
52                            time.localtime(file_stats[stat.ST_ATIME])),
53     'f_ct' : time.strftime("%d/%m/%Y %I:%M:%S %p",
54                            time.localtime(file_stats[stat.ST_CTIME])),
55     'no_of_lines':count,
56     't_char':t_char
57 }
58 
59 print ("\nfile name =", file_info['fname'])
60 print ("file size =", file_info['fsize'] , "bytes")
61 print ("last modified =", file_info['f_lm'])
62 print ("last accessed =", file_info['f_la'])
63 print ("creation time =", file_info['f_ct'])
64 print ("Total number of lines are =", file_info['no_of_lines'])
65 print ("Total number of characters are =", file_info['t_char'])
66 
67 if stat.S_ISDIR(file_stats[stat.ST_MODE]):
68     print ("This a directory")
69 else:
70     print ("This is not a directory\n")
71     print ("A closer look at the os.stat(%s) tuple:" % file_name)
72     print (file_stats)
73     print ("\nThe above tuple has the following sequence:   ")
74     print ("""st_mode (protection bits), st_ino (inode number), 
75     st_dev (device),    st_nlink (number of hard links),    
76     st_uid (user ID of owner),   st_gid (group ID of owner),    
77     st_size (file size, bytes),  st_atime (last access time, seconds since epoch),  
78     st_mtime (last modification time),   st_ctime (time of creation, Windows)"""

find_prime.py
1 '''Author Anurag Kumar(mailto:anuragkumara95@gmail.com)
2 
3 A prime number is a natural number that has exactly two distinct natural number divisors: 1 and itself.
4 
5 #USAGE:
6   - $pythonfind_prime.py <num:int>
7 
8 ##THEORY
9 -Sieve of Eratosthenes(source:wikipedia.com)
10     In mathematics, the sieve of Eratosthenes is a simple, ancient algorithm for finding all prime numbers up to any given limit.
11 
12     It does so by iteratively marking as composite (i.e., not prime) the multiples of each prime, starting with the first prime 
13     number, 2. The multiples of a given prime are generated as a sequence of numbers starting from that prime, with constant 
14     difference between them that is equal to that prime. This is the sieve's key distinction from using trial division to 
15     sequentially test each candidate number for divisibility by each prime.
16 
17     To find all the prime numbers less than or equal to a given integer n by Eratosthenes' method:
18 
19       - Create a list of consecutive integers from 2 through n: (2, 3, 4, ..., n).
20       - Initially, let p equal 2, the smallest prime number.
21       - Enumerate the multiples of p by counting to n from 2p in increments of p, and mark them in the list (these will be 2p, 
22         3p, 4p, ...; the p itself should not be marked).
23       - Find the first number greater than p in the list that is not marked. If there was no such number, stop. Otherwise, let 
24         p now equal this new number (which is the next prime), and repeat from step 3.
25       - When the algorithm terminates, the numbers remaining not marked in the list are all the primes below n.
26 '''
27 import sys
28 
29 def find_prime(num):
30     res_list = []
31     for i in range(2,num+1):
32         if res_list!=[] and any(i%l==0 for l in res_list):
33             continue
34         res_list.append(i)
35     return res_list
36 
37 if __name__=="__main__":
38     if len(sys.argv)!=2: raise Exception("usage - $python find_prime.py <num:int>")
39     try:num = int(sys.argv[1])
40     except ValueError: raise Exception("Enter an integer as argument only.")
41     l = find_prime(num)
42     print(l)

folder_size.py
1 # Script Name   : folder_size.py
2 # Author        : Craig Richards
3 # Created       : 19th July 2012
4 # Last Modified	: 22 February 2016
5 # Version       : 1.0.1
6 
7 # Modifications : Modified the Printing method and added a few comments
8 
9 # Description   : This will scan the current directory and all subdirectories and display the size.
10 
11 import os
12 import sys      # Load the library module and the sys module for the argument vector'''
13 try:
14     directory = sys.argv[1]   # Set the variable directory to be the argument supplied by user.
15 except IndexError:
16     sys.exit("Must provide an argument.")
17 
18 dir_size = 0    # Set the size to 0
19 fsizedicr = {'Bytes': 1,
20              'Kilobytes': float(1) / 1024,
21              'Megabytes': float(1) / (1024 * 1024),
22              'Gigabytes': float(1) / (1024 * 1024 * 1024)}
23 for (path, dirs, files) in os.walk(directory):      # Walk through all the directories. For each iteration, os.walk returns the folders, subfolders and files in the dir.
24     for file in files:                              # Get all the files
25         filename = os.path.join(path, file)
26         dir_size += os.path.getsize(filename)       # Add the size of each file in the root dir to get the total size.
27 
28 fsizeList = [str(round(fsizedicr[key] * dir_size, 2)) + " " + key for key in fsizedicr] # List of units
29 
30 if dir_size == 0: print ("File Empty") # Sanity check to eliminate corner-case of empty file.
31 else:
32   for units in sorted(fsizeList)[::-1]: # Reverse sort list of units so smallest magnitude units print first.
33       print ("Folder Size: " + units)

14     """ print out all 4-digit numbers """
15     numbers = [str(i).zfill(4) for i in range(10000)]

game_o_life.py
1 '''Conway's Game Of Life, Author Anurag Kumar(mailto:anuragkumarak95@gmail.com) 
2 
3 Requirements:
4   - numpy
5   - random
6   - time
7   - matplotlib
8 
9 Python:
10   - 3.5
11 
12 Usage:
13   - $python3 game_o_life <canvas_size:int>
14 
15 Game-Of-Life Rules:
16  
17  1.
18  Any live cell with fewer than two live neighbours
19  dies, as if caused by under-population.
20  2.
21  Any live cell with two or three live neighbours lives
22  on to the next generation.
23  3.
24  Any live cell with more than three live neighbours
25  dies, as if by over-population.
26  4.
27  Any dead cell with exactly three live neighbours be-
28  comes a live cell, as if by reproduction.
29  '''
30 import numpy as np
31 import random, time, sys
32 from matplotlib import pyplot as plt
33 import matplotlib.animation as animation
34 from matplotlib.colors import ListedColormap
35 
36 usage_doc='Usage of script: script_nama <size_of_canvas:int>'
37 
38 choice = [0]*100 + [1]*10
39 random.shuffle(choice)
40 
41 def create_canvas(size):
42     canvas = [ [False for i in range(size)] for j in range(size)]
43     return canvas
44 
45 def seed(canvas):
46     for i,row in enumerate(canvas):
47         for j,_ in enumerate(row):
48             canvas[i][j]=bool(random.getrandbits(1))
49 
50 def run(canvas):
51     ''' This  function runs the rules of game through all points, and changes their status accordingly.(in the same canvas)
52     @Args:
53     --
54     canvas : canvas of population to run the rules on.
55 
56     @returns:
57     --
58     None
59     '''
60     canvas = np.array(canvas)
61     next_gen_canvas = np.array(create_canvas(canvas.shape[0]))
62     for r, row in enumerate(canvas):
63         for c, pt in enumerate(row):
64             # print(r-1,r+2,c-1,c+2)
65             next_gen_canvas[r][c] = __judge_point(pt,canvas[r-1:r+2,c-1:c+2])
66     
67     canvas = next_gen_canvas
68     del next_gen_canvas # cleaning memory as we move on.
69     return canvas.tolist()   
70 
71 def __judge_point(pt,neighbours):
72     dead  = 0
73     alive = 0
74     # finding dead or alive neighbours count.
75     for i in neighbours:
76         for status in i:
77             if status: alive+=1
78             else: dead+=1
79 
80     # handling duplicate entry for focus pt.
81     if pt : alive-=1
82     else : dead-=1
83     
84     # running the rules of game here.
85     state = pt
86     if pt:
87         if alive<2:
88             state=False
89         elif alive==2 or alive==3:
90             state=True
91         elif alive>3:
92             state=False
93     else:
94         if alive==3:
95             state=True
96 
97     return state
98 
99 
100 if __name__=='__main__':
101     if len(sys.argv) != 2: raise Exception(usage_doc)
102    
103     canvas_size = int(sys.argv[1])
104     # main working structure of this module.
105     c=create_canvas(canvas_size)
106     seed(c)
107     fig, ax = plt.subplots()
108     fig.show() 
109     cmap = ListedColormap(['w','k'])
110     try:
111         while True:
112             c = run(c)            
113             ax.matshow(c,cmap=cmap)
114             fig.canvas.draw()
115             ax.cla() 
116     except KeyboardInterrupt:
117         # do nothing.
118         pass

1 # Script Name   : get_info_remoute_srv.py

4 # Last Modified	: -
5 # Version       : 1.0.0
6 
7 # Modifications :
8 
9 # Description   : this will get info about remoute server on linux through ssh connection. Connect these servers must be through keys
10 
11 import subprocess
12 
13 HOSTS = ('proxy1', 'proxy')
14 
15 COMMANDS = ('uname -a', 'uptime')
16 
17 for host in HOSTS:
18     result = []
19     for command in COMMANDS:
20         ssh = subprocess.Popen(["ssh", "%s" % host, command],
21                                shell=False,
22                                stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
23                                stderr=subprocess.PIPE)
24         result.append(ssh.stdout.readlines())
25     print('--------------- ' + host + ' --------------- ')
26     for res in result:
27         if not res:
28             print(ssh.stderr.readlines())
29             break
30         else:
31             print(res)

1 """
2 Author: Ankit Agarwal (ankit167)
3 Usage: python google.py <keyword>
4 Description: Script googles the keyword and opens
5              top 5 (max) search results in separate
6              tabs in the browser
7 Version: 1.0
8 """
9 
10 import webbrowser, sys, pyperclip, requests, bs4
11 
12 def main():
13 	if len(sys.argv) > 1:
14 		keyword = ' '.join(sys.argv[1:])
15 	else:
16 		# if no keyword is entered, the script would search for the keyword
17 		# copied in the clipboard
18 		keyword = pyperclip.paste()
19 
20 	res=requests.get('http://google.com/search?q='+	keyword)
21 	res.raise_for_status()
22 	soup = bs4.BeautifulSoup(res.text)
23 	linkElems = soup.select('.r a')
24 	numOpen = min(5, len(linkElems))
25 
26 	for i in range(numOpen):
27 		webbrowser.open('http://google.com' + linkElems[i].get('href'))
28 
29 if __name__ == '__main__':
30 	main()

kmp_str_search.py
1 """Author Anurag Kumar(mailto:anuragkumarak95@gmail.com)
2     The Knuth-Morris-Pratt Algorithm for finding a pattern within a piece of te$
3     with complexity O(n + m)
4     1) Preprocess pattern to identify any suffixes that are identical to prefix$
5         This tells us where to continue from if we get a mismatch between a cha$
6         and the text.
7     2) Step through the text one character at a time and compare it to a charac$
8         updating our location within the pattern if necessary
9 """
10 def kmp(pattern, text, len_p=None, len_t=None):
11     # 1) Construct the failure array
12     failure = [0]
13     i = 0
14     for index, char in enumerate(pattern[1:]):
15         if pattern[i] == char:
16             i += 1
17         else:
18             i = 0
19         failure.append(i)
20 
21     # 2) Step through text searching for pattern
22     i, j = 0, 0  # index into text, pattern
23     while i < len(text):
24         if pattern[j] == text[i]:
25             if j == (len(pattern) - 1):
26                 return True
27             i += 1
28             j += 1
29 
30         # if this is a prefix in our pattern
31         # just go back far enough to continue
32         elif failure[j] > 0:
33             j = failure[j] - 1
34         else:
35             i += 1
36     return False
37 
38 
39 if __name__ == '__main__':
40 
41     # Test 1)
42     pattern = "abc1abc12"
43     text1 = "alskfjaldsabc1abc1abc12k23adsfabcabc"
44     text2 = "alskfjaldsk23adsfabcabc"
45     assert kmp(pattern, text1) and not kmp(pattern, text2)
46 
47     # Test 2)
48     pattern = "ABABX"
49     text = "ABABZABABYABABX"
50     assert kmp(pattern, text)

lib.py
1 # -*- coding: utf-8 -*-
2 """
3 Created on Mon Feb 26 14:29:11 2018
4 
5 @author: Christian Bender
6 @license: MIT-license
7 
8 This module contains some useful classes and functions for dealing
9 with linear algebra in python.
10 
11 Overview:
12 
13 - class Vector
14 - function zeroVector(dimension)
15 - function unitBasisVector(dimension,pos)
16 - function axpy(scalar,vector1,vector2)
17 - function randomVector(N,a,b)
18 - class Matrix
19 - function squareZeroMatrix(N)
20 - function randomMatrix(W,H,a,b)
21 """
22 
23 
24 import math
25 import random
26 
27 
28 class Vector(object):
29     """
30         This class represents a vector of arbitray size.
31         You need to give the vector components. 
32         
33         Overview about the methods:
34         
35         constructor(components : list) : init the vector
36         set(components : list) : changes the vector components.
37         __str__() : toString method
38         component(i : int): gets the i-th component (start by 0)
39         size() : gets the size of the vector (number of components)
40         euclidLength() : returns the eulidean length of the vector.
41         operator + : vector addition
42         operator - : vector subtraction
43         operator * : scalar multiplication and dot product
44         copy() : copies this vector and returns it.
45         changeComponent(pos,value) : changes the specified component.
46         TODO: compare-operator
47     """
48     def __init__(self,components):
49         """
50             input: components or nothing
51             simple constructor for init the vector
52         """
53         self.__components = components
54     def set(self,components):
55         """
56             input: new components
57             changes the components of the vector.
58             replace the components with newer one.
59         """
60         if len(components) > 0:
61             self.__components = components
62         else:
63             raise Exception("please give any vector")
64     def __str__(self):
65         """
66             returns a string representation of the vector
67         """
68         ans = "("
69         length = len(self.__components)
70         for i in range(length):
71             if i != length-1:
72                 ans += str(self.__components[i]) + ","
73             else:
74                 ans += str(self.__components[i]) + ")"
75         if len(ans) == 1:
76             ans += ")"
77         return ans
78     def component(self,i):
79         """
80             input: index (start at 0)
81             output: the i-th component of the vector.
82         """
83         if i < len(self.__components) and i >= 0:
84             return self.__components[i]
85         else:
86             raise Exception("index out of range")
87     def size(self):
88         """
89             returns the size of the vector
90         """
91         return len(self.__components)
92     def eulidLength(self):
93         """
94             returns the eulidean length of the vector
95         """
96         summe = 0
97         for c in self.__components:
98             summe += c**2
99         return math.sqrt(summe)
100     def __add__(self,other):
101         """
102             input: other vector
103             assumes: other vector has the same size
104             returns a new vector that represents the sum.
105         """
106         size = self.size()
107         result = []
108         if size == other.size():
109             for i in range(size):
110                 result.append(self.__components[i] + other.component(i))
111         else:
112             raise Exception("must have the same size")
113         return Vector(result)
114     def __sub__(self,other):
115         """
116             input: other vector
117             assumes: other vector has the same size
118             returns a new vector that represents the differenz.
119         """
120         size = self.size()
121         result = []
122         if size == other.size():
123             for i in range(size):
124                 result.append(self.__components[i] - other.component(i))
125         else: # error case
126             raise Exception("must have the same size")
127         return Vector(result)
128     def __mul__(self,other):
129         """
130             mul implements the scalar multiplication 
131             and the dot-product
132         """
133         ans = []
134         if isinstance(other,float) or isinstance(other,int):
135             for c in self.__components:
136                 ans.append(c*other)
137         elif (isinstance(other,Vector) and (self.size() == other.size())):
138             size = self.size()
139             summe = 0
140             for i in range(size):
141                 summe += self.__components[i] * other.component(i)
142             return summe
143         else: # error case
144             raise Exception("invalide operand!")
145         return Vector(ans)
146     def copy(self):
147         """
148             copies this vector and returns it.
149         """
150         components = [x for x in self.__components]
151         return Vector(components)
152     def changeComponent(self,pos,value):
153         """
154             input: an index (pos) and a value
155             changes the specified component (pos) with the
156             'value'
157         """
158         #precondition
159         assert (pos >= 0 and pos < len(self.__components))
160         self.__components[pos] = value
161     def norm(self):
162         """
163             normalizes this vector and returns it.
164         """
165         eLength = self.eulidLength()
166         quotient = 1.0 / eLength
167         for i in range(len(self.__components)):
168             self.__components[i] = self.__components[i] * quotient
169         return self
170     def __eq__(self,other):
171         """
172             returns true if the vectors are equal otherwise false.
173         """ 
174         ans = True
175         SIZE = self.size()
176         if (SIZE == other.size()):
177             for i in range(SIZE):
178                 if self.__components[i] != other.component(i):
179                     ans = False
180                     break
181         else:
182             ans = False
183         return ans
184     
185 def zeroVector(dimension):
186     """
187         returns a zero-vector of size 'dimension'
188     """        
189     #precondition
190     assert(isinstance(dimension,int))
191     ans = []
192     for i in range(dimension):
193         ans.append(0)
194     return Vector(ans)
195 
196 
197 def unitBasisVector(dimension,pos):
198     """
199         returns a unit basis vector with a One 
200         at index 'pos' (indexing at 0)
201     """
202     #precondition
203     assert(isinstance(dimension,int) and (isinstance(pos,int)))
204     ans = []
205     for i in range(dimension):
206         if i != pos:
207             ans.append(0)
208         else:
209             ans.append(1)
210     return Vector(ans)
211         
212 
213 def axpy(scalar,x,y):
214     """
215         input: a 'scalar' and two vectors 'x' and 'y'
216         output: a vector
217         computes the axpy operation
218     """
219     # precondition
220     assert(isinstance(x,Vector) and (isinstance(y,Vector)) \
221     and (isinstance(scalar,int) or isinstance(scalar,float)))
222     return (x*scalar + y)
223     
224 
225 def randomVector(N,a,b):
226     """
227         input: size (N) of the vector.
228                random range (a,b)
229         output: returns a random vector of size N, with 
230                 random integer components between 'a' and 'b'.
231     """
232     ans = zeroVector(N)
233     random.seed(None)
234     for i in range(N):
235         ans.changeComponent(i,random.randint(a,b))
236     return ans
237 
238 
239 class Matrix(object):
240     """
241     class: Matrix
242     This class represents a arbitrary matrix.
243     
244     Overview about the methods:
245     
246          __str__() : returns a string representation 
247            operator * : implements the matrix vector multiplication
248                         implements the matrix-scalar multiplication.
249            changeComponent(x,y,value) : changes the specified component.
250            component(x,y) : returns the specified component.
251            width() : returns the width of the matrix
252            height() : returns the height of the matrix
253            operator + : implements the matrix-addition.
254            operator - _ implements the matrix-subtraction
255     """
256     def __init__(self,matrix,w,h):
257         """
258             simple constructor for initialzes 
259             the matrix with components.
260         """
261         self.__matrix = matrix
262         self.__width = w
263         self.__height = h
264     def __str__(self):
265         """
266             returns a string representation of this
267             matrix.
268         """
269         ans = ""
270         for i in range(self.__height):
271             ans += "|"
272             for j in range(self.__width):
273                 if j < self.__width -1:
274                     ans += str(self.__matrix[i][j]) + ","
275                 else:
276                     ans += str(self.__matrix[i][j]) + "|\n"
277         return ans
278     def changeComponent(self,x,y, value):
279         """
280             changes the x-y component of this matrix
281         """
282         if x >= 0 and x < self.__height and y >= 0 and y < self.__width:
283             self.__matrix[x][y] = value
284         else:
285             raise Exception ("changeComponent: indices out of bounds")
286     def component(self,x,y):
287         """
288             returns the specified (x,y) component
289         """
290         if x >= 0 and x < self.__height and y >= 0 and y < self.__width:
291             return self.__matrix[x][y]
292         else:
293             raise Exception ("changeComponent: indices out of bounds")
294     def width(self):
295         """
296             getter for the width
297         """
298         return self.__width
299     def height(self):
300         """
301             getter for the height
302         """
303         return self.__height
304     def __mul__(self,other):
305         """
306             implements the matrix-vector multiplication.
307             implements the matrix-scalar multiplication
308         """
309         if isinstance(other, Vector): # vector-matrix 
310             if (other.size() == self.__width):
311                 ans = zeroVector(self.__height)
312                 for i in range(self.__height):
313                     summe = 0
314                     for j in range(self.__width):
315                         summe += other.component(j) * self.__matrix[i][j]
316                     ans.changeComponent(i,summe)
317                     summe = 0
318                 return ans
319             else:
320                 raise Exception("vector must have the same size as the "
321                 + "number of columns of the matrix!")
322         elif isinstance(other,int) or isinstance(other,float): # matrix-scalar
323             matrix = []
324             for i in range(self.__height):
325                 row = []
326                 for j in range(self.__width):
327                     row.append(self.__matrix[i][j] * other)
328                 matrix.append(row)
329             return Matrix(matrix,self.__width,self.__height)
330     def __add__(self,other):
331         """
332             implements the matrix-addition.
333         """
334         if (self.__width == other.width() and self.__height == other.height()):
335             matrix = []
336             for i in range(self.__height):
337                 row = []
338                 for j in range(self.__width):
339                     row.append(self.__matrix[i][j] + other.component(i,j))
340                 matrix.append(row)
341             return Matrix(matrix,self.__width,self.__height)
342         else:
343             raise Exception("matrix must have the same dimension!")
344     def __sub__(self,other):
345         """
346             implements the matrix-subtraction.
347         """
348         if (self.__width == other.width() and self.__height == other.height()):
349             matrix = []
350             for i in range(self.__height):
351                 row = []
352                 for j in range(self.__width):
353                     row.append(self.__matrix[i][j] - other.component(i,j))
354                 matrix.append(row)
355             return Matrix(matrix,self.__width,self.__height)
356         else:
357             raise Exception("matrix must have the same dimension!")
358     def __eq__(self,other):
359         """
360             returns true if the matrices are equal otherwise false.
361         """
362         ans = True
363         if self.__width == other.width() and self.__height == other.height():
364             for i in range(self.__height):
365                 for j in range(self.__width):
366                     if self.__matrix[i][j] != other.component(i,j):
367                         ans = False
368                         break
369         else:
370             ans = False
371         return ans
372         
373     
374 
375 def squareZeroMatrix(N):
376     """
377         returns a square zero-matrix of dimension NxN
378     """
379     ans = []
380     for i in range(N):
381         row = []
382         for j in range(N):
383             row.append(0)
384         ans.append(row)
385     return Matrix(ans,N,N)
386     
387     
388 def randomMatrix(W,H,a,b):
389     """
390         returns a random matrix WxH with integer components
391         between 'a' and 'b'
392     """
393     matrix = []
394     random.seed(None)
395     for i in range(H):
396         row = []
397         for j in range(W):
398             row.append(random.randint(a,b))
399         matrix.append(row)
400     return Matrix(matrix,W,H)
401             
402         ================

15 class Test(unittest.TestCase):
16     def test_component(self):
17         """
18             test for method component
19         """
20         x = Vector([1,2,3])
21         self.assertEqual(x.component(0),1)
22         self.assertEqual(x.component(2),3)
23         try:
24             y = Vector()
25             self.assertTrue(False)
26         except:
27             self.assertTrue(True)
28     def test_str(self):
29         """
30             test for toString() method
31         """

34     def test_size(self):
35         """
36             test for size()-method

logs.py
1 # Script Name   : logs.py
2 # Author        : Craig Richards
3 # Created       : 13th October 2011
4 # Last Modified	: 14 February 2016
5 # Version		: 1.2
6 #
7 # Modifications	: 1.1 - Added the variable zip_program so you can set it for the zip program on whichever OS, so to run on a different OS just change the locations of these two variables.
8 #               : 1.2 - Tidy up comments and syntax
9 #
10 # Description   : This script will search for all *.log files in the given directory, zip them using the program you specify and then date stamp them
11 
12 import os                   # Load the Library Module
13 from time import strftime   # Load just the strftime Module from Time
14 
15 logsdir = "c:\puttylogs"      # Set the Variable logsdir
16 zip_program = "zip.exe"       # Set the Variable zip_program - 1.1
17 
18 for files in os.listdir(logsdir):                                       # Find all the files in the directory
19 	if files.endswith(".log"):                                      # Check to ensure the files in the directory end in .log
20 		files1 = files + "." + strftime("%Y-%m-%d") + ".zip"    # Create the Variable files1, this is the files in the directory, then we add a suffix with the date and the zip extension
21 		os.chdir(logsdir)                                       # Change directory to the logsdir
22 		os.system(zip_program + " " +  files1 +" "+ files)      # Zip the logs into dated zip files for each server. - 1.1
23 		os.remove(files)                                        # Remove the original log files

magic8ball.py
1 '''Author Anurag Kumar(mailtoanuragkumarak95@gmail.com)
2 Module for implementing the simpest Magic 8 Ball Game.
3 
4 Python:
5   - 3.5
6 
7 Requirements:
8   - colorama
9 
10 Usage:
11   - $python3 magic8ball.py
12 
13 Ask a question, and know the future.
14 '''
15 from time import sleep
16 from random import randint
17 from colorama import Fore, Style
18 
19 # response list..
20 response = [
21     "It is certain",
22     "It is decidedly so",
23     "Without a doubt",
24     "Yes, definitely",
25     "You may rely on it",
26     "As I see it, yes",
27     "Most likely",
28     "Outlook good",
29     "Yes",
30     "Signs point to yes",
31     "Quite possibly so",
32     "Ask again later",
33     "Better not tell you now",
34     "Cannot predict now",
35     "Concentrate and ask again",
36     "Don't count on it",
37     "My reply is no",
38     "My sources say no",
39     "Outlook not so good",
40     "Very doubtful"]
41 
42 # core game...
43 def game():
44     ques = str(input("What is your question? \n").lower())
45     print ("thinking...")
46     sleep(1)
47     idx = randint(0,20)
48     if idx <10: color = Fore.GREEN
49     elif idx>=10 and idx<15: color = Fore.YELLOW
50     else: color = Fore.RED
51     print (color+response[idx]+Style.RESET_ALL+'\n\n')
52     playloop()
53 
54 # looping func...
55 def playloop():
56     ques_again = str(input("Would you like to ask another question? (y/n)\n").lower())
57     if ques_again == 'y':
58         game()
59 
60     elif ques_again == 'n':
61         print("Auf Wiedersehen!")
62 
63     else:
64         print ("What was that?/n")
65         playloop()
66 
67 if __name__=='__main__':
68     game()

meme_maker.py
1 import sys
2 
3 from PIL import ImageDraw, ImageFont, Image
4 
5 
6 def input_par():
7     print('Enter the text to insert in image: ')
8     text = str(input())
9     print('Enter the desired size of the text: ')
10     size = int(input())
11     print('Enter the color for the text(r, g, b): ')
12     color_value = [int(i) for i in input().split(' ')]
13     return text, size, color_value
14     pass
15 
16 
17 def main():
18     path_to_image = sys.argv[1]
19     image_file = Image.open(path_to_image + '.jpg')
20     image_file = image_file.convert("RGBA")
21     pixdata = image_file.load()
22 
23     print(image_file.size)
24     text, size, color_value = input_par()
25     
26     #Font path is given as -->( " Path  to  your  desired  font " )
27     font = ImageFont.truetype("C:\\Windows\\Fonts\\Arial.ttf", size=size)
28 
29     #If the color of the text is not equal to white,then change the background to be white   
30     if((color_value[0] and color_value[1] and color_value[2])!=255):
31         for y in range(100):
32             for x in range(100):
33                 pixdata[x, y] = (255, 255, 255, 255)
34     #If the text color is white then the background is said to be black
35     else:
36         for y in range(100):
37             for x in range(100):
38                 pixdata[x, y] = (0,0, 0, 255)
39     image_file.show()
40 
41     # Drawing text on the picture
42     draw = ImageDraw.Draw(image_file)
43     draw.text((0, 2300), text, (color_value[0], color_value[1], color_value[2]), font=font)
44     draw = ImageDraw.Draw(image_file)
45 
46     print('Enter the file name: ')
47     file_name = str(input())
48     image_file.save(file_name + ".jpg")
49     pass

merge.py
1 # author:zhangshuyx@gmail.com
2 
3 #!/usr/bin/env python
4 # -*- coding=utf-8 -*-
5 
6 import os
7 
8 # define the result filename
9 resultfile = 'result.csv'
10 
11 # the merge func
12 def merge():
13     """merge csv files to one file"""
14 
15     # indicates use of a global variable.
16     global resultfile
17 
18     # use list save the csv files
19     csvfiles = [f for f in os.listdir('.') if f != resultfile  \
20     and (len(f.split('.')) >= 2) and f.split('.')[1]=='csv']
21 
22     # open file to write
23     with open(resultfile,'w') as writefile:
24         for csvfile in csvfiles:
25             with open(csvfile) as readfile:
26                 print('File {} readed.'.format(csvfile))
27                 
28                 # do the read and write
29                 writefile.write(readfile.read()+'\n')
30     print('\nFile {} wrote.'.format(resultfile))
31 
32 # the main program
33 
34 def main():
35     print "\t\tMerge\n\n"
36     print "This program merges csv-files to one file\n"
37     merge()
38 
39 if __name__ == '__main__':
40     main()

move_files_over_x_days.py
1 # Script Name   : move_files_over_x_days.py
2 # Author(s)     : Craig Richards ,Demetrios Bairaktaris
3 # Created       : 8th December 2011
4 # Last Modified : 25 December 2017
5 # Version       : 1.1
6 # Modifications : Added possibility to use command line arguments to specify source, destination, and days. 
7 # Description   : This will move all the files from the src directory that are over 240 days old to the destination directory.
8 
9 import shutil
10 import sys
11 import time
12 import os
13 import argparse
14 
15 usage = 'python move_files_over_x_days.py -src [SRC] -dst [DST] -days [DAYS]'
16 description = 'Move files from src to dst if they are older than a certain number of days.  Default is 240 days'
17 
18 args_parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(usage=usage, description=description)
19 args_parser.add_argument('-src', '--src', type=str, nargs='?', default='.', help='(OPTIONAL) Directory where files will be moved from. Defaults to current directory')
20 args_parser.add_argument('-dst', '--dst', type=str, nargs='?', required=True, help='(REQUIRED) Directory where files will be moved to.')
21 args_parser.add_argument('-days', '--days', type=int, nargs='?', default=240, help='(OPTIONAL) Days value specifies the minimum age of files to be moved. Default is 240.')
22 args = args_parser.parse_args()
23 
24 if args.days < 0:
25 	args.days = 0
26 
27 src = args.src  # Set the source directory
28 dst = args.dst  # Set the destination directory
29 days = args.days #Set the number of days
30 now = time.time()  # Get the current time
31 
32 if not os.path.exists(dst):
33 	os.mkdir(dst)
34 
35 for f in os.listdir(src):  # Loop through all the files in the source directory
36     if os.stat(f).st_mtime < now - days * 86400:  # Work out how old they are, if they are older than 240 days old
37         if os.path.isfile(f):  # Check it's a file
38             shutil.move(f, dst)  # Move the files
39

1 import mechanize

3 from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
4 
5 # Create a Browser
6 browser = mechanize.Browser()
7 
8 # Disable loading robots.txt
9 browser.set_handle_robots(False)
10 
11 browser.addheaders = [('User-agent',
12                  'Mozilla/4.0 (compatible; MSIE 5.0; Windows 98;)')]
13 
14 movie_title = raw_input("Enter movie title: ")
15 
16 movie_types = ('feature', 'tv_movie', 'tv_series', 'tv_episode', 'tv_special',
17     'mini_series', 'documentary', 'game', 'short', 'video', 'tvshort')
18 
19 # Navigate
20 browser.open('http://www.imdb.com/search/title')
21 
22 # Choose a form
23 browser.select_form(nr=1)
24 
25 browser['title'] = movie_title
26 
27 # Check all the boxes of movie types
28 for type in movie_types:
29     browser.find_control(type='checkbox',nr=0).get(type).selected = True
30 
31 # Submit
32 fd   = browser.submit()
33 soup = BeautifulSoup(fd.read(),'html5lib')
34 
35 
36 # Updated from td tag to h3 tag
37 for div in soup.findAll('h3', {'class': 'lister-item-header'}, limit=1):
38     a = div.findAll('a')[0]
39     hht = 'http://www.imdb.com' + a.attrs['href']
40     print(hht)
41     page  = urllib2.urlopen(hht)

multiplication_table.py
1 from sys import argv # import argment variable 
2 
3 script, rows, columns = argv #define rows and columns for the table and assign them to the argument variable
4 
5 
6 def table(rows, columns):
7 	for i in range(1, int(rows) + 1 ): #it's safe to assume that the user would mean 12 rows when they provide 12 as an argument, b'coz 12 will produce 11 rows
8 		print ("\t", i,)
9 
10 	print ("\n\n")
11 
12 	for i in range(1, int(columns) + 1 ):
13 		print (i),
14 		for j in range(1, int(rows) + 1 ):
15 			print ("\t",i*j,)
16 		print ("\n\n")
17 		
18 table(rows, columns)

nDigitNumberCombinations.py
1 # ALL the combinations of n digit combo
2 def nDigitCombinations():
3 	try:
4 		npow = 10**n
5 		numbers=[]
6 		for code in range(npow):
7 			code=str(code).zfill(n)
8 			numbers.append(code)
9 	except:
10 		# handle all other exceptions
11 		pass    
12 	return(numbers)

new_script.py
1 # Script Name	: new_script.py
2 # Author			: Craig Richards
3 # Created			: 20th November 2012
4 # Last Modified	:
5 # Version			: 1.0
6 
7 # Modifications	:
8 
9 # Description		: This will create a new basic template for a new script
10 
11 import os				# Load the library module
12 import sys				# Load the library module
13 import datetime		# Load the library module
14 
15 text = '''You need to pass an argument for the new script you want to create, followed by the script name.  You can use
16 	-python	: Python Script
17 	-bash	: Bash Script
18 	-ksh	: Korn Shell Script
19 	-sql	: SQL Script'''
20 
21 if len(sys.argv) < 3:
22   print text
23   sys.exit()
24 
25 if '-h' in sys.argv or '--h' in sys.argv or '-help' in sys.argv or '--help' in sys.argv:
26   print text
27   sys.exit()
28 else:
29   if '-python' in sys.argv[1]:
30     config_file = "python.cfg"
31     extension = ".py"
32   elif '-bash' in sys.argv[1]:
33     config_file = "bash.cfg"
34     extension = ".bash"
35   elif '-ksh' in sys.argv[1]:
36     config_file = "ksh.cfg"
37     extension = ".ksh"
38   elif '-sql' in sys.argv[1]:
39     config_file = "sql.cfg"
40     extension = ".sql"
41   else:
42     print 'Unknown option - ' + text
43     sys.exit()
44 
45 confdir = os.getenv("my_config")
46 scripts = os.getenv("scripts")
47 dev_dir = "Development"
48 newfile = sys.argv[2]
49 output_file = (newfile + extension)
50 outputdir = os.path.join(scripts,dev_dir)
51 script = os.path.join(outputdir, output_file)
52 input_file = os.path.join(confdir,config_file)
53 old_text = " Script Name	: "
54 new_text = (" Script Name	: " + output_file)
55 if not(os.path.exists(outputdir)):
56   os.mkdir(outputdir)
57 newscript = open(script, 'w')
58 input = open(input_file, 'r')
59 today = datetime.date.today()
60 old_date = " Created	:"
61 new_date = (" Created	: " + today.strftime("%d %B %Y"))
62 
63 for line in input:
64   line = line.replace(old_text, new_text)
65   line = line.replace(old_date, new_date)
66   newscript.write(line)

nmap_scan.py
1 # Script Name		: nmap_scan.py
2 # Author				: Craig Richards
3 # Created				: 24th May 2013
4 # Last Modified		:
5 # Version				: 1.0
6 
7 # Modifications		:
8 
9 # Description			: This scans my scripts directory and gives a count of the different types of scripts, you need nmap installed to run this
10 
11 import nmap			# Import the module
12 import optparse		# Import the module
13 
14 
15 def nmapScan(tgtHost, tgtPort):									# Create the function, this fucntion does the scanning
16   nmScan = nmap.PortScanner()
17   nmScan.scan(tgtHost, tgtPort)
18   state = nmScan[tgtHost]['tcp'][int(tgtPort)]['state']
19   print "[*] " + tgtHost + " tcp/" + tgtPort + " " + state
20 
21 
22 def main():																								# Main Program
23   parser = optparse.OptionParser('usage%prog ' + '-H <host> -p <port>')		# Display options/help if required
24   parser.add_option('-H', dest='tgtHost', type='string', help='specify host')
25   parser.add_option('-p', dest='tgtPort', type='string', help='port')
26   (options, args) = parser.parse_args()
27   tgtHost = options.tgtHost
28   tgtPorts = str(options.tgtPort).split(',')
29 
30   if (tgtHost == None) | (tgtPorts[0] == None):
31     print parser.usage
32     exit(0)
33 
34   for tgtPort in tgtPorts:				# Scan the hosts with the ports etc
35     nmapScan(tgtHost, tgtPort)
36 
37 
38 if __name__ == '__main__':
39   main()

notepad_support.py
1 #! /usr/bin/env python
2 #
3 # Support module generated by PAGE version 4.10
4 # In conjunction with Tcl version 8.6

8 import sys
9 import sqlite3
10 
11 try:
12     from Tkinter import *
13 except ImportError:
14     from tkinter import *

16 try:
17     import ttk
18     py3 = 0
19 except ImportError:
20     import tkinter.ttk as ttk
21     py3 = 1
22 
23 # connect with database 'data.db'
24 connection = sqlite3.connect("data.db")
25 
26 # creates a cursor (pointer) to the data base
27 cursor = connection.cursor()
28 
29 search = False
30 
31 results = []
32 
33 index = 0
34 
35 def delete_button(p1):
36     global index
37     global results
38     global cursor
39 
40     # fetch id of the current note
41     id = results[index][0]
42 
43     sql_command = """ DELETE FROM notes WHERE id = {0}; """
44     sql_command = sql_command.format(id)
45 
46     cursor.execute(sql_command)
47 
48     connection.commit()
49 
50 
51 def create_button(p1):
52     """
53         for creating a new database
54     """
55     global cursor
56 
57     sql_command = """
58     CREATE TABLE notes ( 
59     id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY, 
60     title TEXT, 
61     note TEXT);"""
62 
63     try:
64         cursor.execute(sql_command)
65         w.errorOutput.configure(text="")
66     except:
67         w.errorOutput.configure(text="The database already exists")
68 
69 def add_button(p1):
70     # for manipulating the data base
71     global cursor
72     global connection
73     if (len(w.inputTitle.get()) > 0 and len(w.inputNotice.get(1.0,END)) > 0):
74         w.errorOutput.configure(text="")
75         title = w.inputTitle.get()
76         note = w.inputNotice.get(1.0,END)
77         sql_command = """INSERT INTO notes (title,note) VALUES ("{0}","{1}"); """
78         sql_command = sql_command.format(title,note)
79         cursor.execute(sql_command)
80         connection.commit()
81     else:
82         w.errorOutput.configure(text="Please fill the fields. ")
83 
84 def back_button(p1):
85     global search
86     global results
87     global index
88     
89     w.errorOutput.configure(text="")
90     index -= 1
91     if (index >= 0 and index < len(results)):
92         w.outputNotice.delete(1.0,END)
93         w.outputNotice.insert(1.0,results[index][2])
94             
95     
96 
97 def clear_button(p1):
98     """
99         This function is for the clear button.
100         This will clear the notice-input field
101     """
102     w.inputNotice.delete(1.0, END)
103 
104 def exit_button(p1):
105     """
106         function for the exit button.
107         this will exit the application.
108     """
109     sys.exit(0)
110 
111 def search_button(p1):
112     global cursor
113     global results
114     global index
115     w.errorOutput.configure(text="")
116     sql_command = """ SELECT * FROM notes WHERE title LIKE "%{0}%";"""
117     sql_command = sql_command.format(w.inputSearchTitle.get())
118     try:
119         cursor.execute(sql_command)
120         results = cursor.fetchall()
121         w.errorOutput.configure(text=str(len(results)) + " results")
122         index = 0
123         if (index >= 0 and index < len(results)):
124             w.outputNotice.delete(1.0,END)
125             w.outputNotice.insert(1.0,results[index][2])
126     except:
127         w.errorOutput.configure(text ="Please create at first a database.")
128         
129 
130 
131 def next_button(p1):
132     global results
133     global index
134     index += 1
135     if (len(w.inputSearchTitle.get()) > 0):
136         if (index >= 0 and index < len(results)):
137             w.outputNotice.delete(1.0,END)
138             w.outputNotice.insert(1.0,results[index][2])
139             
140     else:
141         w.errorOutput.configure(text="Please fill the search field. ")
142

17         'architecture',

34 class bcolors:
35     HEADER = '\033[95m'
36     OKBLUE = '\033[94m'
37     OKGREEN = '\033[92m'
38     WARNING = '\033[93m'
39     FAIL = '\033[91m'
40     ENDC = '\033[0m'
41     BOLD = '\033[1m'
42     UNDERLINE = '\033[4m'
43 
44 
45 for key in profile:
46     if hasattr(pl, key):
47         print(key + bcolors.BOLD + ": " + str(getattr(pl, key)()) + bcolors.ENDC)

get_ip_gui
1 #!/usr/bin/env python3
2 # -*- coding: utf-8 -*-
3 
4 #**************** Modules Require *****************#
5 from tkinter import *
6 import socket
7 from urllib.request import urlopen
8 
9 #**************** Get IP commands *****************#
10 #control buttons
11 def get_wan_ip():
12     try :
13         #get ip from http://ipecho.net/plain as text 
14         wan_ip=urlopen('http://ipecho.net/plain').read().decode('utf-8')
15         res.configure(text='Wan IP is : '+wan_ip,fg='#600')
16     except :
17         res.configure(text='Problem in source : http://ipecho.net/plain',fg='red')
18 #get local ip     
19 def get_local_ip():
20     try:
21         lan_ip=(socket.gethostbyname(socket.gethostname()))
22         res.configure(text='Local IP is : '+lan_ip,fg='#600') 
23     except:
24         res.configure(text='Unkown Error',fg='#red') 
25 #**************** about control button *****************#
26 #show about info and change the button command and place
27 def about():
28     global close_app,frame,info
29     about_app.destroy()
30     frame=Frame(root,width=350,height=2,bg='blue')
31     frame.grid(row=2,column=0,columnspan=4)
32     info=Label(root,text="""
33     Practice Python 
34     Take idea from here :
35     https://github.com/geekcomputers/Python/blob/master/myip.py
36     """,fg='#02F')
37     info.grid(row=3,column=0,columnspan=4,padx=5)    
38     close_app=Button(root,text='Close',command=close_about,bg='#55F')
39     close_app.grid(row=4,column=0,columnspan=4,pady=5)    
40 #remove about info and remove close button then return about button in orignal place
41 def close_about():
42     global frame,about_app,info
43     info.destroy()
44     frame.destroy()
45     close_app.destroy()
46     about_app=Button(root,text='about',command=about)
47     about_app.grid(row=1,column=2,padx=5,pady=5,sticky=W)    
48 
49 #**************** Tkinter GUI *****************#
50 root=Tk()    
51 root.title ('Khaled programing practice')
52 #all buttons
53 res=Label(root,text='00.00.00.00',font=25)
54 res_wan_ip=Button(root,text='Get Wan IP',command=get_wan_ip)
55 res_local_ip=Button(root,text='Get Local IP',command=get_local_ip)
56 about_app=Button(root,text='about',command=about)
57 quit_app=Button(root,text='quit',command=quit,bg='#f40')
58 #method grid to install the button in window

62 about_app.grid(row=1,column=2,padx=5,pady=5,sticky=W)

password_cracker.py
1 # Script Name	: password_cracker.py
2 # Author		: Craig Richards
3 # Created		: 20 May 2013
4 # Last Modified	:
5 # Version		: 1.0
6 
7 # Modifications	:
8 
9 # Description	: Old school password cracker using python
10 
11 from sys import platform as _platform
12 
13 # Check the current operating system to import the correct version of crypt
14 if _platform in ["linux", "linux2", "darwin"]: # darwin is _platform name for Mac OS X
15     import crypt # Import the module
16 elif _platform == "win32":
17     # Windows
18     try:
19        import fcrypt # Try importing the fcrypt module
20     except ImportError:
21        print 'Please install fcrypt if you are on Windows'
22 
23 
24 def testPass(cryptPass):	  # Start the function
25   salt = cryptPass[0:2]
26   dictFile = open('dictionary.txt','r')	  # Open the dictionary file
27   for word in dictFile.readlines():	  # Scan through the file
28     word = word.strip('\n')
29     cryptWord = crypt.crypt(word, salt)	  # Check for password in the file
30     if (cryptWord == cryptPass):
31       print "[+] Found Password: "+word+"\n"
32       return
33   print "[-] Password Not Found.\n"
34   return
35 
36 
37 def main():
38   passFile = open('passwords.txt')		  # Open the password file
39   for line in passFile.readlines():	   # Read through the file
40     if ":" in line:
41       user = line.split(':')[0]
42       cryptPass = line.split(':')[1].strip(' ') # Prepare the user name etc
43       print "[*] Cracking Password For: " + user
44       testPass(cryptPass)				# Call it to crack the users password
45 
46 if __name__ == "__main__":
47   main()

ping_servers.py
1 # Script Name		: ping_servers.py

7 # Modifications		: 1.1 - 14th May 2012 - CR Changed it to use the config directory to store the server files

9 # Description			: This script will, depending on the arguments supplied will ping the servers associated with that application group.
10 
11 import os						  	# Load the Library Module
12 import subprocess				# Load the Library Module
13 import sys							# Load the Library Module
14 
15 filename = sys.argv[0]																# Sets a variable for the script name
16 if '-h' in sys.argv or '--h' in sys.argv or '-help' in sys.argv or '--help' in sys.argv:	# Help Menu if called
17     print '''
18 You need to supply the application group for the servers you want to ping, i.e.
19     dms
20     swaps
21 
22 Followed by the site i.e.
23     155
24     bromley'''
25     sys.exit(0)
26 else:
27 
28     if (len(sys.argv) < 3): 																# If no arguments are passed,display the help/instructions on how to run the script
29         sys.exit ('\nYou need to supply the app group. Usage : ' + filename + ' followed by the application group i.e. \n \t dms or \n \t swaps \n then the site i.e. \n \t 155 or \n \t bromley')
30 
31     appgroup = sys.argv[1]															# Set the variable appgroup as the first argument you supply
32     site = sys.argv[2]																	# Set the variable site as the second argument you supply
33 
34     if os.name == "posix":															# Check the os, if it's linux then
35         myping = "ping -c 2 "															# This is the ping command
36     elif os.name in ("nt", "dos", "ce"):											# Check the os, if it's windows then
37         myping = "ping -n 2 "															# This is the ping command
38 
39     if 'dms' in sys.argv:																	# If the argument passed is dms then
40       appgroup = 'dms'																	# Set the variable appgroup to dms
41     elif 'swaps' in sys.argv:															# Else if the argment passed is swaps then
42       appgroup = 'swaps'																# Set the variable appgroup to swaps
43 
44     if '155' in sys.argv:																	# If the argument passed is 155 then
45       site = '155'																			# Set the variable site to 155
46     elif 'bromley' in sys.argv:															# Else if the argument passed is bromley
47       site = 'bromley'																	# Set the variable site to bromley
48 
49 logdir = os.getenv("logs")															# Set the variable logdir by getting the OS environment logs
50 logfile = 'ping_' + appgroup + '_' + site + '.log'										# Set the variable logfile, using the arguments passed to create the logfile
51 logfilename = os.path.join(logdir, logfile)											# Set the variable logfilename by joining logdir and logfile together
52 confdir = os.getenv("my_config")													# Set the variable confdir from the OS environment variable - 1.2
53 conffile = (appgroup + '_servers_' + site + '.txt')									# Set the variable conffile - 1.2
54 conffilename = os.path.join(confdir, conffile)									# Set the variable conffilename by joining confdir and conffile together - 1.2
55 
56 f = open(logfilename, "w")															# Open a logfile to write out the output
57 for server in open(conffilename):													# Open the config file and read each line - 1.2
58     ret = subprocess.call(myping + server, shell=True, stdout=f, stderr=subprocess.STDOUT)	# Run the ping command for each server in the list.
59     if ret == 0:																				# Depending on the response
60       f.write (server.strip() + " is alive" + "\n")									# Write out that you can receive a reponse
61     else:
62       f.write (server.strip() + " did not respond" + "\n")						# Write out you can't reach the box
63 
64 print ("\n\tYou can see the results in the logfile : " + logfilename);	# Show the location of the logfile
